Free Talk

Random Thoughts in July

— Wen

The seventh month of the lunar calendar is indeed the best time of the year, the so-called "Cool weather and cold weather" season. Therefore, folk legends and stories about July are particularly numerous. It is natural for poets, with their sensitivity, to feel melancholy about the desolation of the autumn wind. As for why ordinary people, lacking such acute sensitivity, would also sing praises of July, it seems that it is none other than the fact that the busy farming season is over, the weather is cool, and they can enjoy the fruits of their labor in peace. However, in modern China, where floods and droughts turn bountiful harvests into disasters and the countryside goes bankrupt, how farmers feel about autumn may still be a question.

The most poetic of the folk legends in July is, of course, the story of the Cowherd and the Weaver Girl on the Double Seventh Festival. Lafcadio Hearn (Koizumi Yakumo) has a book of "Galaxy Stories," which recounts the elegant customs in Japanese villages on the evening of the Double Seventh Festival, where people hang five-colored poems on bamboo poles and throw them into clear streams to be carried away by the water. He also translated several ancient Japanese songs in it.

Next is the Ullambana Festival on the fifteenth day of July. The origin of this custom is likely based on the story of Maudgalyāyana saving his mother from the Ullambana Sutra. However, it later became increasingly elaborate, involving intricate techniques such as carving wood and bamboo, and cutting colored sugar and wax to create shapes of flowers and leaves. In Japanese villages, on the evening of the fifteenth of July, there is also a custom of men and women dancing wildly until dawn, called Bon Odori. I have had the opportunity to witness this several times in Nikko and Shiobara and found that the primitive dancing of the farmers, combined with the atmosphere of rustic men and women singing and joking, created a kind of indescribable joy. I wonder if these surviving customs from July in Japan are our own domestic products from the Sui and Tang dynasties. I would very much like to consult scholars of textual research on this point.

Further embellishments derived from the story of Maudgalyāyana saving his mother include the releasing of river lanterns and the planting of Jizo incense on the thirtieth of July. In the past, when I resided on the north bank of Shichahai in Beiping, every autumn, walking past the Jingye Nunnery in Jishuitan would remind me of Wang Cihui's quatrain "River Lanterns at Jingye Nunnery on an Autumn Night." I have heard that Shaoxing has large-scale Maudgalyāyana opera troupes and scripts. I wonder if this Maudgalyāyana opera is also an amateur pastime for farmers in Shaoxing during July.

Nankou Apples

— Li Tiao

Nankou not only produces apples but also many other fruits such as apricots, grapes, crabapples, and peaches. However, when I vowed to spend a day in Nankou, it happened to be the season when apples were ripening.

As soon as the train stopped, the hawkers' shouts outside the platform pierced my ears like scolding. I don't understand why Northerners are so extreme in their emotions, even shouting sales pitches so loudly, as if threatening people to buy their goods. Some set up stalls outside the wooden fence, clinging to the fence and shouting at the passengers on the train. Others, with one hand clinging to the fence and their feet on the horizontal bars, leaned their bodies inward, while the other hand stretched out their goods to get closer to the customers getting off the train. They thought that being near the water tower, they would be the first to benefit. The customers would surely take care of their business first. However, this kind intention was often not accepted. Customers getting off the train would often glance at them disdainfully and run to the stalls outside the fence to bargain. Thus, they had no choice but to shout and wave their outstretched hands holding the goods to the next customer.

The goods, apart from the occasional cooked chicken, soy milk, rice porridge, and buns, were mostly fruit. And what I want to talk about are apples. As soon as you leave Beiping to the west, the scenery becomes scorched yellow. But Nankou has round, reddish-pink apples, like the delicate cheeks of a sixteen-year-old girl, displayed in baskets and hampers, which are truly beautiful.

Fruit is a famous product of Nankou. This place has fresh and cheap seasonal fruits on the market for three seasons of the year. Apples are priced at three dimes for a large basket and two dimes for a small basket. Those who are not good at bargaining can get a large basket for two dimes, while those who are good at bargaining can get it for one dime and a half. Furthermore, shrewd old-timers would rather buy by the catty, as the price per catty is about the same, but it avoids the drawback of having rotten or inferior apples at the bottom. A large basket contains about eleven or twelve catties, using the sixteen-tael scale.

Fruit becomes more expensive as soon as it leaves Nankou, probably because fruit gradually loses its freshness after leaving the place of origin, so it becomes more valuable. Speaking of which, Nankou has the Ping Sui Railway connecting it to Beiping, and the train can arrive in an hour. However, the trains are often diverted for military use, and passenger trains are often delayed by three or four hours. Freight trains, because they have to wait for military trains to be towed, only get a locomotive to pull them after a delay of one or two days. They also have to give way to military trains on the road, and the locomotive has to go to pull military trains. So, when the fruit can be transported from Nankou to Beiping is unknown.

Nankou is surrounded by mountains, with fruit trees growing abundantly in the mountains, blooming and bearing fruit in beautiful scenery. Nankou also has ancient battlefields, with fortresses still standing and bullet marks still visible. There is also a memorial tower for fallen soldiers built of earth and stone, standing on the right side of the road. There are many such memorial towers in China - for the revolution, for martyrs, for suppressing △, for suppressing X - and many more can be built in the future. After visiting, I felt that the memorial towers in other places are built even better than this one.

There are many military trains and the apples are very cheap. The soldiers going west are going to fight against the "fake resistance against Japan," which is very good. The more military trains, the cheaper the apples, which is very beneficial for those passing by.

Now that there is no trouble over there, the military trains will be coming back! The apples will probably still be cheap.

"Satisfaction" and "Cannot Write"

— Sun Yong

It is natural that people who are satisfied with everything cannot write articles. Therefore, creation is precisely a symbol of distress.

However, in present-day China, it is quite strange that the so-called "literati" can actually utter the words "extremely satisfied" about this kind of life.

However, an ignorant and unknowledgeable young master actually said in a small newspaper: "I am a person who is extremely satisfied with life. I feel that people come into the world to enjoy themselves, not to suffer..." Naturally, the young master who relies on his ancestors' legacy and his wife's dowry to enjoy life has nothing to be dissatisfied with. But has he ever thought that in China, the vast majority of people do indeed come to suffer, not to enjoy? Some young people may boast that they are "truly handsome" gigolos, but it is also very clear that there are not many daughters of prime ministers with millions of dollars of dowries waiting for people to seduce them on the Shanghai Bund!

The young master also said: "I feel that suffering is also a privilege, and suffering is a destiny. Why can I endure suffering, but you cannot? ... If I have to suffer, I will suffer, and I do not want to express any dissatisfaction." This is actually not worth "writing out," because first, it reminds me of a satirical cartoon: a capitalist giving a speech to several workers, his speech being, "God said that mankind did not come into the world just for bread." (General idea). Secondly, I am also thinking of the inert brother-like-ist who believes that there is no need to destroy, no need to transform, and that the status quo is the best of all.

I looked again at his reasons for satisfaction. According to himself, he is neither "economically well-off" nor has he "never suffered," but it is because he is "worthy of himself" and "faithful to himself." To say "worthy of oneself" and "faithful to oneself" in more popular terms is called "selfish and self-interested." Of course, "selfish and self-interested" cannot write the poetry of a "prophet." Moreover, in present-day China, with even a little humanity, one cannot only care about oneself.

However, the young master's slogan is:

Satisfaction with life, I cannot write;

A world of enjoyment, I cannot write;

One joy in life, I cannot write;

There are many articles; I cannot write.

If you cannot write, then there is no need to embarrass yourself, you should go back to your old business, mixing cosmetics and creating seemingly understandable but actually meaningless poems, stealing the title of "poet" for your own amusement!

Miscellaneous Mountain Tales (Continued)

— A Ying

㈢ Answering Articles

When I saw the title "Answering Articles" in Ming Ren and Jiang Nanrong's "Chats of Half-Rustic Villagers," I was very happy. This refers to the affairs of Wang Zhongyi, Duke Ji. The text says: "Wang Zhongyi, Duke Ji, with his great achievements and outstanding virtues, stood out in his generation. Whenever someone asked for poetry or prose, he would compose it with a stroke of his pen, without giving it much thought. He once said to people, 'The honest writing of the North is not a model, it is only answering, even attaching the draft.' This shows the Duke's sincerity. However, the Duke's worthiness of remembrance does not depend on this."

"Only answering," this sentence is absolutely straightforward and incisive. In the collections of writers of the past, there are always inevitably articles that are "only answering," sometimes even many. Some writers, such as Zheng Banqiao, have even openly cursed against this, but what effect does it have? Writers still have to write articles that are "only answering." Such articles are not called "only answering" now. The most common term is "ghost-busting," "ghost-busting articles," or more elegantly, "occasional pieces," "fulfilling the matter." Literature has been revolutionized, literary language has become vernacular, but this kind of "fulfilling the matter," a disguised form of "only answering" articles, has consistently existed. Even a sage like Hu Shi, who opposed writing such articles, has not been able to avoid it to this day, let alone others? This kind of "only answering" article not only exists now but is also developing. It has developed to the point where people calling themselves writers are writing "only answering" articles to kill, to sing praises, to vent personal grievances. It can be said that in addition to the boring "only answering" articles for entertaining friends, a new system has now been added! "Blood-sucking articles"! Blood-sucking indeed, shameless indeed! (The End)

Women (III)

— Shen Congwen

The patient, hearing this question, seemed to be reminded by it of unpleasant impressions from another time and another event, and asked the woman in return, "When are you leaving?"

The woman did not answer immediately, but raised her head and looked at the patient with her bright eyes for a while. Then, she drooped her head powerlessly, sighed softly, and said to herself, "When am I leaving?"

The patient understood the reason and said:

"It's alright not to leave! In August in XX, the scenery is beautiful everywhere. And didn't you say that when I get better, get out of the hospital, you would accompany me to spend time in XX?"

"To stay there for half a month? The leaves on the mountain there are extremely beautiful, I like those trees. If you leave, I don't want to go there alone. Why do you want to leave?"

The woman lowered her head, saying with a sense of sadness, "Why do I want to leave? I really don't know!"

The patient said:

"I remembered a poem of yours. That poem called 'The Mystery of the Seasonal Flowers,' I remember you so..." Unable to decide whether to say "lonely" or "sentimental," he changed his tone and said to the woman, "It must be very cold outside, why don't you wear your purple clothes?"

The woman pretended not to hear this sentence, listlessly twisting her gloves. After a while, she asked again, "After you get out of the hospital, do you plan to go to the mountain, or not?"

The patient seemed to have recalled everything from the past month in the hospital, and his heart softened. He quietly said, "If you don't leave, you come to the mountain with me, wouldn't that be good? You have to leave."

"I have to leave, yes, I have to leave."

"I want you to accompany me!"

"You don't need me to accompany you!"

"But you know..."

"But you..."

Nothing more needed to be said; both were rendered speechless by one thing.

She loved him, he understood; he did not love her, she also understood. The problem was in this. For three years, each person's position had remained the same, without much change.

Their ages differed by about seven years. This gap separated the friendship between these two people, causing them to stop at a certain thin curtain. Both were gazing at the other's emotional state, but often remained silently in a daze, unable to open their arms and allow the other to weakly and willfully lie in those arms.

(Summer, a hot, oppressive, and tiring summer.)

Three years ago, at a summer seaside academic conference in XX in the South, fifty young women and seventy young men gathered, setting up tents by the sea to live through the summer. These young men and women all came from various universities. In the morning, they gathered in the shade of trees and in temporary mat sheds to listen to lectures from famous professors from Beiping. In the afternoon, they would go to the seaside bathing beach for seawater baths. In the evening, they would put on plays, watch movies, and hold small group discussions and dance parties, while also gathering in smaller groups. On the beach and on the small hilltops, torches were often lit, and piles of firewood were burned to indicate the location of the camp to those boating at sea and those lost in the mountains.

Among the women, there was an outstanding figure. The daughter of a XX chief, born out of wedlock, and a third-year student at XX University. This woman was not only pure and beautiful in character and scholarship, but also exceptionally beautiful in appearance. She was skilled in swimming, horseback riding, boating, and ball games, surpassing others in every way. Moreover, she was exceptionally lively and lacked any frivolous habits. She was gentle and kind in her dealings with others, and was therefore admired by the entire group. In particular, one young professor and one middle-aged professor were extremely admiring of this woman. However, at that time, the girl seemed indifferent to all the courtesies. It was as if this person felt that she should always be admired by everyone, always belong to everyone, and could not be exclusively occupied by one person. Therefore, she remained solitary, never softened by any love.

Amateur Weekly

The Future of the US National Recovery Movement

— Ms. Xiao Chengyi

The economic panic of 1933 swept through the imperialist countries and their colonies. Even America, the so-called "Gold Dollar Empire," was caught in the whirlpool. In February of this year, just days after President Roosevelt took office, a very serious banking holiday financial crisis erupted, not only affecting all 48 states of the United States, but also impacting the entire world. Countless US industrial and commercial enterprises were affected, causing cash flow problems and leading to shutdowns and bankruptcies, which in turn exacerbated the severity of unemployment and panic, making it impossible to resolve. At the same time, the agricultural panic caused by the fall in agricultural prices further interacted with the financial panic, making it even more profound.

After the financial crisis broke out, President Roosevelt took emergency measures, promulgating various mandatory decrees to temporarily curb the powerful financial storm with extraordinary means. He then implemented the so-called "National Recovery Movement" to restore the prosperity of the golden age of capitalism in 1927. But can this really succeed? Let us first see how he is doing this "recovery movement," and then discuss its success or failure.

The main aspect of the "Recovery Movement" is to carry out large-scale construction projects in order to reduce and curb the increase in unemployment. The plan includes finding new mines to dig and afforest, as well as immediately starting to manufacture dozens of warships with the massive tonnage permitted by the "Naval Treaty" to stimulate production industries. It is said that the implementation of this "Recovery Movement" can provide employment for 500,000 workers. However, this alone reveals the emptiness of the so-called "National Recovery Movement." The United States now has 12 million unemployed workers, and the result of this "Recovery Movement" of large-scale construction is only to provide employment for 500,000 workers. Isn't this just a drop in the bucket? Although the effect is not equal to zero, it can be generally seen. In particular, a large part of the large-scale construction projects belong to shipbuilding, from which it can be further known that the fundamental purpose of the so-called "Recovery Movement" is not "recovery" at all. Rather, it is based on Japan's urgent attack on China, and the balance of the open-door policy in China cannot be maintained and is being monopolized by Japan. At the same time, due to the increasing urgency of the international situation, and the possibility of a world war for the re-division of colonies in the declining period of capitalism breaking out at any moment, they have had to vigorously expand their military equipment and throw a so-called "National Recovery Movement" smoke screen to cover up.

Now, even if we take a step back and admit that the purpose of the "National Recovery Movement" is for "recovery," what is the progress of the movement? The Reuters dispatch in the Shenbao of the 17th of this month carries the following: "The National Recovery Movement has now entered the second stage, and the government is encountering even greater difficulties. For example, the oil, iron, steel, and coal industries are constantly arguing about working hours and wage regulations, ┆┆ President Roosevelt is now actively trying to mediate the stalemate through the Supreme Recovery Administration Committee ┆┆ The Administration Committee is discussing various methods, one of which is to order male and female students who have recently graduated from school to return to school to alleviate the serious situation of unemployment. ┆" But regarding the dispute over working hours and wage regulations, is it safeguarding the interests of the capitalists?

Or is it favoring the workers? Due to the devaluation of currency and the rise in prices, the real wages of workers have decreased a lot, and life has become extremely difficult. Recently, 60,000 male and female garment workers in New York, New Jersey, and Connecticut have declared a general strike to demand increased wages and improved treatment, and there is a tendency to involve other industries. Resolving this dispute over wages and working hours is undoubtedly extremely difficult. In particular, the Administration Committee's plan to order students who have recently graduated from school to re-enter school in order to alleviate the serious situation of unemployment further shows that the "Recovery Movement" has no ability to provide effective and active relief for the unemployment problem. In short, the American economic panic caused by the inherent shortcomings of capitalism itself cannot be solved by President Roosevelt's "National Recovery Movement." For the same reason, the world economic recession, production decline, unemployment panic, trade decline, and the increase in all panic figures, due to the increase in tariff barriers in various countries, and the fierce struggle of currency and exchange rate policies caused by the fall in gold prices, making the situation increasingly worse, cannot be solved by the World Economic Conference. Therefore, the adjournment of the World Economic Conference without any results is not surprising.

An Extra in a Motion Picture Company

The Dead Man in the Coffin

— Yao Shiquan

People who work as extras in motion picture companies shoot films day and night. Sometimes, when you receive a notice to shoot a film at nine o'clock in the morning, you have to be at the company at eight o'clock. It is very common to shoot from nine o'clock until nine o'clock the next morning. Being confined in this unventilated lead house all day long is okay in cold weather, but it is unbearable in hot weather. Under the thirty-odd high-intensity electric lights, each lamp has a heat of at least like an electric stove. The sweltering heat of June is the period when we extras work desperately. It is like a dead man being confined in a coffin, unable to feel a single breeze or breathe in any air. Sometimes, the director does not care about your life or death. In hot weather, he wants to shoot a scene set in cold weather, so you have to put on a leather coat and wear a leather hat. Although you are sweating profusely, feeling dizzy, and extremely hot, in order to look real, the large stove in the set has to be turned on. The director orders you to say, "The plot is like this, you have to pretend to be very afraid of the cold and walk towards the stove to warm yourself." Then, you must naturally walk forward and re-bake your already stifled body. If you don't do this, how can you get the two yuan payment? Your heart is burning with fever,

Echoes of Self-Employment Introductions

Bingjun: We intend to invite you to serve as a social science teacher. We hope you will come to discuss the matter immediately. (Pang Zihang, Mingqiang Middle School, Maixing Road)

Ms. Qing: Please contact the following places: 1. Liu Wozhong, Post Office Box 159, this port, 2. Pang Zihang, Mingqiang Middle School, Shixing Road, and 3. Cao Yinyun, Sales Department, Bunnemann Company, 41 Sichuan Road.

Ms. Shi: Please contact Mr. Zhao at No. 65 Yuanfuli, Baoding Road, Tangshan Road, in person.

Mmes. Jing and Shi: Please indicate your mailing address. (Ju, 111 Meibai Road)

On the outside, you still have to pretend to be shivering from the cold. The female stars have people fanning them, and the director has ice cream and Dutch water, but what do we bit players have? Nothing but blood and sweat! Even if you are burning up with heat, like a steamed bun coming out of the steamer, the female star will still joke and say, "You look like a red-hot fat pig's head." At that time, you must smile ┆ smile ┆ and smile! And you had better answer wittily and say, "I look like a frozen lion's head." Then,

Page 22

They will laugh. This is not humiliation, it is supreme glory, because you bit players are not worthy of their delicate smiles!

The director's murderous decree continues to be issued: "Prepare the camera! Quick! ┆┆ Dead man! ┆┆ Pig! Hurry up and get closer, add coal to the fire, pretend to be afraid of the cold and shivering." At this time, our Lord God the director! He is truly like an all-powerful official, binding us insignificant commoners on the rack of torture, and we can only resign ourselves to fate. After a shot is finished, "Cut! Turn off the lights. Miss XX is hot, isn't she? Someone, fan her! ┆┆ Dutch water!" In the day and night by the blood-sucking machine, this sound is the most pleasant and the one we hear most often.

When the filming is over, it is dawn, and then you receive your wages. The two yuan payment is deducted by the agency for six jiao, and then four jiao for meals, leaving only one yuan in hand. This amount is not small, I think it is a lot. If you can shoot for eight or nine days a month, you won't starve to death even if you are hungry! For a day and a night, you risk your life, are scolded like a pig and a dog, have a sore back and legs, and are dizzy. Only then can you go home to rest and sleep. The journey home of more than ten miles can only be made on my two bicycles that don't cost money, and I run back quickly.

"Revolutionary Writer Gorky"

— Ms. Zhuang Keneng

丨Published by Shenghai Bookstore, priced at one yuan and two jiao丨

I spent three evenings reading "Revolutionary Writer Gorky." Undoubtedly, this book tells the story of Gorky's life and is a biography of him. However, I believe that it should not be regarded as an ordinary biography and read lightly. It should be seen as a good model for young people to emulate and a cornerstone for inspiration. Because although he was born in such a dark, damp, and muddy society at that time, he was still able to use his wise eyes to see the cruelty, shamelessness, stupidity of people, and the strangeness of various behaviors at that time. Even in his childhood, he witnessed everything and was able to stir his heartstrings, arousing his injustice and anger. He did not consider his humble origins as vulgar and shameful, but instead hardened his will because of the hardships he had personally experienced. He never succumbed to external temptations or yielded to violence. He always resisted violence and sympathized with the weak. He started his first job at the age of ten because his eccentric superior (cook) insisted that he read books to him, which aroused his interest in reading. After that, he seemed to be addicted and refused to be separated from books. Finally, he read extensively and became a homeless person wandering along the Volga River! He once drifted to work as a worker on the docks, a porter, and an apprentice cook on a ship! One day, he climbed to the highest peak of the Russian literary world and became a revolutionary writer who is famous all over the world today. This is not accidental. He has a history of struggle, an uncompromising spirit, a firm will, a keen eye, a cry for the welfare of the masses at the cost of self-sacrifice, and he does not collude with the treacherous and insidious people around him. What a great and admirable personality! No wonder Mr. Lu Xun said, "This book is really a good gift for Chinese youth." Therefore, I hope that every young person can accept this solemn gift.

Timely Article

July 7th

— Chen Tiaoyue

The slender crescent moon hung on the willow branch by the ditch. The early autumn night wind carried the mournful cries of autumn insects "jiji". Several dogs lying on the threshing floor preparing to spend the night, impatiently shook their heads at the moonlight a couple of times, and then lay still.

Ah, the early autumn night is desolate, but tonight there is a performance at the Dongyue Temple 丨 "The Cowherd and the Weaver Girl" 丨 Tonight is July 7th.

Looking in through the paper window of that thatched hut, under the dim candlelight, Meixiang had already brewed her mother's medicine. She frowned and tasted it herself to check the temperature, and then held it in both hands to her mother's bedside.

"Mom!" Her mother's eyes were tightly closed, her cheeks were flushed, and her pale forehead was covered with cold sweat. Usually, when she was sick and unable to get out of bed, she would constantly moan, moaning in pain, moaning in distress. This time, she did not moan, she was always so quiet, like the desolate early autumn night.

But tonight there is a performance at the Dongyue Temple 丨 "The Cowherd and the Weaver Girl"! Tonight is July 7th.

Meixiang put her mouth to her mother's ear:

"Mom, the medicine is brewed. The doctor said that this prescription will have some effect. Mom, why are you always silent? The doctor said: you are too worried. Mom, my brother shouldn't be in too much danger."

Alas! Alas! Alas! That child Shengfu ┆ I told him early on ┆ not to go with that group ┆ to make trouble, and now he has been arrested for more than ten days, with no news at all. I am afraid he is mostly killed. Alas! Alas! Alas! My life will not be long either, worrying about you, this young girl, young ┆" Old people cannot afford to get sick. Once they get sick, they cannot even speak clearly.

"Mom, don't worry. Brother won't be killed. The officials also understand the suffering of the poor, and it is not a crime for workers to reasonably demand a wage increase from the boss! Mom, the medicine is getting cold, drink it."

Meixiang's mother, who was suffering from third-stage pulmonary tuberculosis, stretched her thin neck and just drank the medicine when she "poo" spit it out again.

"Tap, tap, tap," the sound of knocking on the door.

"Who is it?" Meixiang asked towards the door while wiping the medicine stains on her mother's chin.

"It's me!"

"I'm holding my mom!"

"Aren't you going to the Dongyue Temple? I came to find you specifically."

Glancing at her mother's face on her wrist, "I'm not going, my mom is very sick, you go alone. Don't forget to bring some lotus root to my mom."

"┆┆Little vixen┆┆Making people run for nothing┆┆"

"Do you hate me? ┆"

"┊┊" The voice outside disappeared.

The heart of a lung patient is often clear.

"Who told you to go to the Dongyue Temple?"

"Wang San's daughter from the previous village went!"

The hearts of young girls are the same, like a lotus flower just emerging from the water, swaying in the early autumn night wind, but Meixiang's heart is desolate.

"Will my brother really not be killed? Is it a crime to jointly demand a wage increase from the boss? Will the officials really understand the suffering of the poor? Old and sick mother, ┆┆ young self ┆┆?" Thinking, thinking, the fire of hope was blown away by the early autumn night wind. Thousands of sharpened arrows pierced through the heart one by one, and then pierced through the back one by one. The liquid from the heart turned into tears, sour and bitter, one by one, row by row. The candle on the table was also shedding tears.

An elderly person seriously ill is like a dying candle facing this early autumn night wind, and will be extinguished in a moment. The slender crescent moon outside the house, with its waist bent, moved lightly and quietly climbed to the roof ridge of the Earth God Temple. Ah, the early autumn night! It is desolate, desolate, but tonight there is a performance at the Dongyue Temple! 丨 "The Cowherd and the Weaver Girl" 丨 Tonight is July 7th.

Reader's Opinion Box

Goodbye, "Outdated" Amateur Weekly Editor!

Editor: Please don't be shocked that a young man you've never met is writing you such a letter. If you are not "self-righteous," then please calmly read this letter!

I feel that the entire society is in a chaotic and dark period. The sharpening of class distinctions is causing the petty bourgeoisie to gradually decline. As a result, what is reflected in literature and art is only the groaning and dying cries of the petty bourgeoisie in the period of decline, either lamenting poverty or indulging in wine, sex, and women. I find it strange why the petty-bourgeois literati are just decadent all day long, willingly heading down the path of decline, and why there is no one with a rebellious mood to shout loudly!

Since you, sir, started editing the Amateur Weekly, it has indeed made me very excited. Although I don't know you personally, sir, I know that you must be a petty-bourgeoisie, but one who is unwilling to be暴 and is shouting loudly. I don't need to use nauseating words to compliment you, sir, but I think your publication is the most impressive supplement in the major newspapers. I admire your shouting spirit very much, sir, but I think your consciousness is not sufficient and not complete, which makes me deeply regret it. Maybe I have my own views, and you, sir, have your own views. "People have different aspirations, how can they be forced?" "Those who have different paths do not conspire with each other." But I believe that there is only one truth, and one plus one will never be equal to a number other than two!

In order to point out the error of your, sir, consciousness, I will first quote your, sir, words as follows:

丨June 11th "The Way Out for the Poor"!

"We hope that the gentlemen of the government should reflect on themselves and understand the difficulty of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's forty years of revolution,

and clearly understand the root cause of all unrest in society! The number of poor people is increasing. By referring to the Premier's will in this regard and working hard on relief efforts, there may be a glimmer of hope for the country's future. ┆┆"

丨July 2nd "The Nation's Future in the Mouths of Elementary School Teachers!"

"We teach and hope that the gentlemen of the government who are now actually responsible should ask themselves in the quiet of the night "┆┆┆"┆┆"

The above only extracts two paragraphs and is not taking things out of context. The original text is too long to record.

From the above two paragraphs, it seems that your, sir, method of saving the country is only a kind of "hope," a vague "hope," hoping that the gentlemen of the government will have a change of heart. I

Special Self-Employment Introduction

Six Sisters Group

— Ms. Shan

We six are all sisters, with no uncles, no brothers, and no husbands. Our father was a famous painter, but he has now passed away. We are all university graduates. The total age is one hundred and forty-two years, with an average of about twenty-four years each. As for scholarship and talent, although we cannot compare with the French brother writers Alexandre Dumas and Alexandre Dumas Jr., we are all proficient in Chinese and Western painting, crafts, poetry, Chinese shorthand, and

Go, and can speak Shanghainese and Mandarin. We are all willing to serve as art teachers in middle schools, whether "hired separately" or "hired together" is acceptable. Mailing address: c/o this publication.

Page 23

I think your, sir, earnest advice and loud shouts are truly admirable and pitiable, which makes me suddenly think of the loyal ministers and righteous servants in ancient history who directly advised the emperor and knelt and cried. If the emperor is gracious and accepts the loyal advice, then the country can be prosperous and the loyal ministers can be promoted and ennobled. But if there is a king who does not know good from bad, and is furious and kills the loyal ministers, and is even angrier and exterminates the nine clans, then things will be terrible!

You, sir, believe that the rise and fall of the nation depends on a single thought of the gentlemen of the government. Isn't this completely idealistic argument coming from your, sir, mouth a great joke to the world? We can naturally forgive your, sir, difficulties. In this era, it is truly said that trouble comes from the mouth, and criticizing in the stomach is a crime. We cannot speak freely, but can we just cover up our conscience and make insincere remarks!

In such a stormy era, in such an era of widespread poverty and hardship, we still use the word "hope" to comfort ourselves, deceive ourselves, and anesthetize ourselves. We truly feel that we are too pitiful, as pitiful as a lamb hoping for the master's forgiveness.

Finally, I hope that you, sir, before the gentlemen of the government reflect on themselves and examine their consciences in the quiet of the night, you yourself may also reflect on yourself and examine your conscience in the quiet of the night. Think carefully about whether the young man's words are right or wrong!

The Pain of a Small Employee

Goodbye, sir! Goodbye, "Outdated" Amateur Weekly Editor!

A reader of Amateur Weekly

The Unbearable Favor

— Ms. Fang

Part One

I wake up very late every day. This isn't due to inherent laziness, but because my utterly exhausted body needs a moment of rest. I feel like even this rest is so short, so I usually don’t crawl out of bed until after nine o'clock.

As soon as I roll out of bed, as always, my white-haired, pitiful mother immediately stumbles over with a basin of water for me to wash my face. Then, she presents a cup of hot water and two cold buns on a three-legged table. After washing my face, applying a layer of powder, tidying up my clothes, I wolf down the buns in a few bites, drink a cup of hot water, and rush out the door, sprinting to our restaurant. We must be at the restaurant before half-past nine to do our work. If we're even a minute late, the restaurant owner will fly into a rage and scold us mercilessly. And if business is a little slow that day, we're even more unlucky. The owner's threats are definitely not just a momentary outburst. He says, "Useless! Even ghosts are afraid to look at you, who else would want you to serve them? Today's sales will be deducted from your pay, and tomorrow you'll be dismissed." Alas, we dare not say a word back. If we provoke his temper, our jobs will truly be lost. We can only swallow our tears and, returning late at night, cry under the covers.

Upon entering the restaurant, we must first check our assigned areas—tables, chairs, tablecloths, oil and vinegar bottles—to see if they are dirty. If so, we must wipe them clean again with fresh water. We must prepare everything that is missing, one by one. Although the busboys have swept the floor once, we must inspect it again. After taking care of these chores, we must go to the kitchen to check all the ingredients for the day. We must carefully note which dishes were not available yesterday and which new dishes have been added, so we can properly serve our esteemed guests. By this time, it's probably almost eleven o'clock, and we finally have time to wait for the honored guests to arrive.

The busiest time is usually from three o'clock in the afternoon, with the most bustling being around nine o'clock in the evening. At the small, three-foot-wide kitchen door, a dozen female colleagues rush back and forth, carrying trays. If you're not experienced, you'll easily bump into someone and drop a tray of dishes. When the honored guests are toasting and eating, needless to say, we must accompany them, attending to them diligently and enthusiastically. In order to receive their generous tips, we must not only be clever with our words and pleasant in our appearance, but also endure all their insulting words and actions. No, they even call it affectionate favor! Heavens, are waitresses really just a type of prostitute? If it weren't for my aged and feeble parents and my three young siblings, if it weren't for the livelihood of my family, why would I be a waitress and subject myself to the favor of others? Too much favor is something a poor person cannot bear. To put it another way, if the monthly salary the restaurant owner paid could support these five lives without starving, why would I risk being treated like a toy by these honored guests, just to get a few tips?

The entire day's work leaves my body exhausted. I wish I could just use this floor as a mattress. Finally, the clock strikes one in the morning. The esteemed guests gradually depart, leaving their seats empty. We wait for the owner to calculate the day's earnings, watching his expressions of joy and anger. We sisters divide the tips bestowed upon us by the guests. Finally, we hear the owner's usual shout, "Come earlier tomorrow!" and we part ways, each heading home.

"Mom! Open the door!"

She's still awake, waiting for me.

"Xiao Ying, you're back! It's already past two o'clock."

The Art of "Having Fun"

— Zhen Yuan

Part Two

The life of a waitress in Peiping is very hard. Although their income varies greatly, most can only barely make ends meet. Their wages are very low, at most three or four yuan per month, relying entirely on tips. However, they argue fiercely over even a few cents difference in wages, because the amount of wages determines their rank. Those with higher ranks can get more tips. In addition to the tips they are rightfully entitled to, they can also sometimes get special tips. Special tips are extra tips given secretly by the customers to one person alone. Needless to say, this is only the privilege of those waitresses with special abilities. There are also those who are very good at attracting customers and have special contracts with the owner, such as getting a certain percentage of all tips themselves. For example, in one restaurant in Peiping, there are more than twenty male and female employees, among whom one waitress gets four-tenths of the tips alone, leaving the remaining six-tenths to be divided among everyone else.

Speaking of how they treat customers, they treat those who are mainly there to eat the same way as the male waiters. But those who are mainly there to "have fun" require a lot of dealing with. A customer who is mainly there to "have fun" doesn't immediately order food upon entering. They always start with a pot of tea, slowly sipping it, and constantly calling the waitress into the room. Sometimes they ask for a napkin, sometimes they say the tea is cold, saying this and that, asking all sorts of questions. Only after several tens of minutes will they finally order dishes. When it comes time to order, they pretend to order while talking nonsense, sometimes taking ten or twenty minutes to order just two or three dishes. If she gets impatient or walks away because other customers are calling, he will immediately clang his bowl and chopsticks, forcing her to come back. The dishes he orders are always a few that go well with wine. When the dishes arrive, he slowly drinks his wine, just like when he was drinking tea, constantly calling people and asking for this and that, all to make the waitress stay in the room longer so he can "have fun." After the wine, he orders a few rice dishes. He eats the rice slowly. After the rice, he orders another pot of tea and continues to drink it slowly. It often takes three or four hours to eat a meal. When waitresses encounter this type of customer, they not only can't get angry, but they must also treat them especially well, because first of all, it's their duty, and second of all, offending a valued customer is a big deal. However, there are also those who especially welcome this type of customer, because that's where the special tips come from.

Eating Waitresses

— Ji Zhongyan

Part Three

In Peiping, the only businesses that hire waitresses are restaurants. The owners cleverly combine the four elements of drinking, eating, men, and women, truly seizing upon a wonderful theme. It even has a hint of humorous philosophy.

In reality, the number of stores in Peiping that hire waitresses is quite limited, mostly just new small restaurants and cafes. The old restaurants, aside from those that closed after the government moved south like Rui Ji Guang He Ju, etc., the currently open ones like Dong Xin Lou, Fu Quan Guan, Quan Ju De, Zhong Xin Tang, Yu Hua Tai, Bian Yi Fang, etc., seem to have not been affected by this so-called trend and continue to operate as they always have. Judging from the situation, their business may even be better than those restaurants that hire waitresses. Therefore, waitresses in Peiping are completely utilized by the owners as a kind of "living signboard" for advertising. At the entrance of stores that hire waitresses, you can easily find two equally sized red paper signs. If one side says "Fresh Stewed Mutton," then the other side, without a doubt, is "Young Waitresses."

Where to even begin with this...?

A certain authority in Peiping once issued a notice only allowing waitresses to wear plain blue cloth gowns, which is just ridiculous. But that's all they can prohibit. They certainly can't further restrict their shoes, socks, and makeup, so some of the waitresses inevitably have to spread the color on their faces.

What's especially outrageous is that a group of utterly bored literati (?) openly wrote novels like this in the newspaper: "Hey! Old Li, want to go eat waitresses?"

"Sure..."

Can waitresses be eaten? How strange! Therefore, many nursery rhymes have appeared in the Peiping market: "Waitresses, they're really not bad (not bad meaning not rotten). Cost three mao, give one yuan. Just don't want the old ladies!"
